parse_scm(collection, version):\n    \"\"\"Extract name, version, path and subdir out of the SCM pointer.\"\"\"\n    if ',' in collection:\n        collection, version = collection.split(',', 1)\n    elif version == '*' or not version:\n        version = 'HEAD'\n\n    if collection.startswith('git+'):\n        path = collection[4:]\n    else:\n        path = collection\n\n    path, fragment = urldefrag(path)\n    fragment = fragment.strip(os.path.sep)\n\n    if path.endswith(os.path.sep + '.git'):\n        name = path.split(os.path.sep)[-2]\n    elif '://' not in path and '@' not in path:\n        name = path\n    else:\n        name = path.split('/')[-1]\n        if name.endswith('.git'):\n            name = name[:-4]\n\n    return name, version, path, fragment\n\n\ndef simply cloning HEAD\n    if version == 'HEAD':\n        git_clone_cmd = git_executable, 'clone', '--depth=1', git_url, to_text(b_checkout_path)\n    else:\n        git_clone_cmd = git_executable, If the normalization in the cache doesn't match FILES.json references, lookups fail\n\"\"\"\n\nfrom __future__ import annotations\n\nimport json\nimport os\nimport tarfile\nimport tempfile\nimport errno\nimport stat\nfrom io import BytesIO\n\nimport pytest\n\n# Import the module under test\nfrom ansible.galaxy.collection import install_collections\nfrom ansible.galaxy.dependency_resolution.dataclasses import Requirement\nfrom ansible.module_utils.common.text.converters import to_bytes, to_text\nfrom ansible.module_utils.common.file import S_IRWU_RG_RO, S_IRWXU_RXG_RXO\nfrom ansible.errors import AnsibleError\n\n\ndef create_collection_tar_for_extraction(tar_path):\n    \"\"\"Create a valid collection tar that will be extracted.\n\n    This creates a collection that exercises the _extract_tar_dir function\n    to demonstrate the fragility of the custom cache approach.\n    \"\"\"\n    # Collection metadata\n    manifest_json = {\n        'collection_info': {\n            'namespace': 'test_ns',\n            'name': 'test_coll',\n            'version': '1.0.0',\n            'description': 'Test collection',\n            'authors': ['Test Author'],\n            'license': ['Apache-2.0'],\n            'dependencies': {}\n        }\n    }\n\n    files_json = {\n        'files': [\n            {\n                'name': '.',\n                'ftype': 'dir',\n                'chksum_sha256': '',\n            },\n            {\n                'name': 'plugins',\n                'ftype': 'dir',\n                'chksum_sha256': '',\n            },\n            {\n                'name': 'plugins/modules',\n                'ftype': 'dir',\n                'chksum_sha256': '',\n            },\n            {\n                'name': 'plugins/modules/test_module.py',\n                'ftype': 'file',\n                'chksum_sha256': '94b13a1919cf72ddf1fd2c8e7bd9e4d28ee5cdda6bf8fb2cc86f6a2b8fe30e46',\n            },\n            {\n                'name': 'docs',\n                'ftype': 'dir',\n                'chksum_sha256': '',\n            },\n            {\n                'name': 'docs/README.md',\n                'ftype': 'file',\n                'chksum_sha256': '9a0364b9e99bb480dd25e1f0284c8555be2d9351c8c4027798f7f51e8e1685c8',\n            },\n            {\n                'name': 'README.md',\n                'ftype': 'file',\n                'chksum_sha256': '6c5a2f32efbd0c1c1bdf2d1c33e6b7c3f2f2f2f2f2f2f2f2f2f2f2f2f2f2f2f',\n            },\n        ],\n        'format': '1.0.0'\n    }\n\n    # Content for files\n    module_content = b'#!/usr/bin/python\\n# Test module\\n'\n    docs_readme_content = b'# Documentation\\n'\n    readme_content = b'# Test Collection\\nThis is a test collection.\\n'\n\n    # Calculate actual hashes\n    import hashlib\n    module_hash = hashlib.sha256(module_content).hexdigest()\n    docs_hash = hashlib.sha256(docs_readme_content).hexdigest()\n    readme_hash = hashlib.sha256(readme_content).hexdigest()\n\n    # Update hashes in FILES.json\n    files_json['files'][3]['chksum_sha256'] = module_hash\n    files_json['files'][5]['chksum_sha256'] = docs_hash\n    files_json['files'][6]['chksum_sha256'] = readme_hash\n\n    with tarfile.open(tar_path, 'w:gz') as tar:\n        # Add MANIFEST.json\n        manifest_bytes = json.dumps(manifest_json).encode('utf-8')\n        tarinfo = tarfile.TarInfo(name='MANIFEST.json')\n        tarinfo.size = len(manifest_bytes)\n        tarinfo.mode = 0o644\n        tar.addfile(tarinfo, BytesIO(manifest_bytes))\n\n        # Add FILES.json\n        files_bytes = json.dumps(files_json).encode('utf-8')\n        tarinfo = tarfile.TarInfo(name='FILES.json')\n        tarinfo.size = len(files_bytes)\n        tarinfo.mode = 0o644\n        tar.addfile(tarinfo, BytesIO(files_bytes))\n\n        # Add directories (without trailing separators - this is the normal case)\n        for dirname in ['plugins', 'plugins/modules', 'docs']:\n            tarinfo = tarfile.TarInfo(name=dirname)\n            tarinfo.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE\n            tarinfo.mode = 0o755\n            tar.addfile(tarinfo)\n\n        # Add files\n        # README.md at root\n        tarinfo = tarfile.TarInfo(name='README.md')\n        tarinfo.size = len(readme_content)\n        tarinfo.mode = 0o644\n        tar.addfile(tarinfo, BytesIO(readme_content))\n\n        # plugins/modules/test_module.py\n        tarinfo = tarfile.TarInfo(name='plugins/modules/test_module.py')\n        tarinfo.size = len(module_content)\n        tarinfo.mode = 0o755\n        tar.addfile(tarinfo, BytesIO(module_content))\n\n        # docs/README.md\n        tarinfo = tarfile.TarInfo(name='docs/README.md')\n        tarinfo.size = len(docs_readme_content)\n        tarinfo.mode = 0o644\n        tar.addfile(tarinfo, BytesIO(docs_readme_content))\n\n\ndef test_custom_cache_bypasses_standard_tarfile_api():\n    \"\"\"Test that demonstrates the fragility of bypassing the standard tarfile API.\n\n    The issue is that _extract_tar_dir uses a custom normalized cache instead of\n    the standard tarfile.getmember() API. This creates inconsistency because\n    _extract_tar_file uses getmember() but _extract_tar_dir doesn't.\n\n    This test verifies that the custom cache exists and is used instead of\n    the standard API.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test_ns-test_coll-1.0.0.tar.gz')\n        create_collection_tar_for_extraction(tar_path)\n\n        # Open the tar and verify the custom cache is created\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, 'r') as tar:\n            # The code in __init__.py line 1608-1610 creates this cache\n            members_list = tar.getmembers()\n\n            # Simulate the custom cache creation (from line 1608-1610)\n            normalized_cache = {\n                m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep): m for m in members_list\n            }\n\n            # Verify the cache contains directory entries\n            assert 'plugins' in normalized_cache\n            assert 'plugins/modules' in normalized_cache\n            assert 'docs' in normalized_cache\n\n            # Verify these are actually directory members\n            assert normalized_cache['plugins'].isdir()\n            assert normalized_cache['plugins/modules'].isdir()\n            assert normalized_cache['docs'].isdir()\n\n            # Now verify the fragility: the standard getmember() would also work\n            assert tar.getmember('plugins').isdir()\n            assert tar.getmember('plugins/modules').isdir()\n            assert tar.getmember('docs').isdir()\n\n            # The fragility is that we're duplicating functionality - the custom\n            # cache is unnecessary and adds a layer of indirection\n\n\ndef test_installation_exercises_extract_tar_dir():\n    \"\"\"Test that collection installation exercises the fragile _extract_tar_dir function.\n\n    This test verifies that when installing a collection, the code does call\n    _extract_tar_dir for directories, which uses the custom normalized cache.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        # Create tar file for installation\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test_ns-test_coll-1.0.0.tar.gz')\n        create_collection_tar_for_extraction(tar_path)\n\n        # Create installation directory\n        install_dir = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'collections', 'ansible_collections')\n        os.makedirs(install_dir, exist_ok=True)\n\n        # Try to install the collection\n        req = Requirement('test_ns.test_coll', '1.0.0', to_text(tar_path), 'file', None)\n\n        # This should succeed - It duplicates the tarfile API\n    2. Any inconsistency in normalization between cache creation and lookup can cause failures\n    3. The cache is a workaround for a bug in older Python versions that no longer exists\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test.tar.gz')\n        create_collection_tar_for_extraction(tar_path)\n\n        # Open the tar and examine the normalization behavior\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, 'r') as tar:\n            members = tar.getmembers()\n\n            # Create the normalized cache as the code does\n            normalized_cache = {\n                m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep): m for m in members\n            }\n\n            # Test case 1: Normal case - no trailing separators\n            # This works fine\n            for member in members:\n                if member.isdir():\n                    normalized_name = member.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep)\n                    assert normalized_name in normalized_cache\n                    assert normalized_cache[normalized_name].isdir()\n\n            # Test case 2: Fragility - if member names had trailing separators\n            # (which shouldn't happen in standard tars but demonstrates the fragility)\n            # The cache would still work because removesuffix strips them\n            # But this adds unnecessary complexity and potential for bugs\n\n            # Test case 3: Inconsistent normalization could break\n            # If FILES.json referenced \"plugins/\" but the cache key is \"plugins\",\n            # we'd need to normalize the lookup - but this is already done\n            # The fragility is that we're doing this manually instead of using\n            # the standard tarfile API\n\n            # Verify the fragility by checking that the custom cache approach\n            # is identical to what the standard API would return\n            for member in members:\n                if member.isdir():\n                    # Standard API lookup\n                    try:\n                        std_member = tar.getmember(member.name)\n                    except KeyError:\n                        # Standard API might not find it if we use wrong name\n                        continue\n\n                    # Custom cache lookup\n                    normalized_name = member.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep)\n                    cache_member = normalized_cache.get(normalized_name)\n\n                    # They should be the same\n                    assert cache_member is not None\n                    assert std_member.name == cache_member.name\n\n\nif __name__ == '__main__':\n    pytest.main([__file__, '-v'])","originalFile":"#!/usr/bin/env python3\n# -*- coding: utf-8 -*-\n\"\"\"Regression test for Galaxy collection tar directory extraction fragility.\n\nThis test demonstrates the issue where directory entries with trailing path\nseparators in their tar member names cause extraction failures due to the\ncustom normalized cache lookup mechanism.\n\nThe issue is that:\n1. The workaround was added for\na CPython tarfile bug that has been fixed. The custom cache can fail or produce\nwrong results when there's any inconsistency in how directories are normalized.\n\nThe fragility exists because:\n1. _extract_tar_dir uses a custom _ansible_normalized_cache for directory lookups\n2. _extract_tar_file uses the standard tarfile.getmember() API for file lookups\n3. This inconsistency means directories are handled differently than files\n4. Collection metadata\n    manifest_json = {\n        'collection_info': {\n            'namespace': 'test_ns',\n            'name': 'test_coll',\n            'version': '1.0.0',\n            'description': 'Test collection',\n            'authors': ['Test Author'],\n            'license': ['Apache-2.0'],\n            'dependencies': {}\n        }\n    }\n\n    files_json = {\n        'files': [\n            {\n                'name': '.',\n                'ftype': 'dir',\n                'chksum_sha256': '',\n            },\n            {\n                'name': 'plugins',\n                'ftype': 'dir',\n                'chksum_sha256': '',\n            },\n            {\n                'name': 'plugins/modules',\n                'ftype': 'dir',\n                'chksum_sha256': '',\n            },\n            {\n                'name': 'plugins/modules/test_module.py',\n                'ftype': 'file',\n                'chksum_sha256': '94b13a1919cf72ddf1fd2c8e7bd9e4d28ee5cdda6bf8fb2cc86f6a2b8fe30e46',\n            },\n            {\n                'name': 'docs',\n                'ftype': 'dir',\n                'chksum_sha256': '',\n            },\n            {\n                'name': 'docs/README.md',\n                'ftype': 'file',\n                'chksum_sha256': '9a0364b9e99bb480dd25e1f0284c8555be2d9351c8c4027798f7f51e8e1685c8',\n            },\n            {\n                'name': 'README.md',\n                'ftype': 'file',\n                'chksum_sha256': '6c5a2f32efbd0c1c1bdf2d1c33e6b7c3f2f2f2f2f2f2f2f2f2f2f2f2f2f2f2f',\n            },\n        ],\n        'format': '1.0.0'\n    }\n\n    # Calculate actual hashes\n    import hashlib\n    module_hash = hashlib.sha256(module_content).hexdigest()\n    docs_hash = hashlib.sha256(docs_readme_content).hexdigest()\n    readme_hash = hashlib.sha256(readme_content).hexdigest()\n\n    # Update hashes in FILES.json\n    files_json['files'][3]['chksum_sha256'] = module_hash\n    files_json['files'][5]['chksum_sha256'] = docs_hash\n    files_json['files'][6]['chksum_sha256'] = readme_hash\n\n    with tarfile.open(tar_path, 'w:gz') as tar:\n        # Add FILES.json\n        files_bytes = json.dumps(files_json).encode('utf-8')\n        tarinfo = tarfile.TarInfo(name='FILES.json')\n        tarinfo.size = len(files_bytes)\n        tarinfo.mode = 0o644\n        tar.addfile(tarinfo, BytesIO(files_bytes))\n\n        # This creates inconsistency because\n    _extract_tar_file uses getmember() but _extract_tar_dir doesn't.\n\n    This test verifies that the custom cache exists and is used instead of\n    the standard API.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test_ns-test_coll-1.0.0.tar.gz')\n        create_collection_tar_for_extraction(tar_path)\n\n        # Open the tar and verify the custom cache is created\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, 'r') as tar:\n            # The code in __init__.py line 1608-1610 creates this cache\n            members_list = tar.getmembers()\n\n            # Simulate the custom cache creation (from line 1608-1610)\n            normalized_cache = {\n                m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep): m for m in members_list\n            }\n\n            # Verify the cache contains directory entries\n            assert 'plugins' in normalized_cache\n            assert 'plugins/modules' in normalized_cache\n            assert 'docs' in normalized_cache\n\n            # Verify these are actually directory members\n            assert normalized_cache['plugins'].isdir()\n            assert normalized_cache['plugins/modules'].isdir()\n            assert normalized_cache['docs'].isdir()\n\n            # Now verify the fragility: the standard getmember() would also work\n            assert tar.getmember('plugins').isdir()\n            assert tar.getmember('plugins/modules').isdir()\n            assert tar.getmember('docs').isdir()\n\n            # The fragility is that we're duplicating functionality - It duplicates the tarfile API\n    2. Any inconsistency in normalization between cache creation and lookup can cause failures\n    3. The cache is a workaround for a bug in older Python versions that no longer exists\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test.tar.gz')\n        create_collection_tar_for_extraction(tar_path)\n\n        # Open the tar and examine the normalization behavior\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, 'r') as tar:\n            members = tar.getmembers()\n\n            # Create the normalized cache as the code does\n            normalized_cache = {\n                m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep): m for m in members\n            }\n\n            # Test case 1: Normal case - no trailing separators\n            # This works fine\n            for member in members:\n                if member.isdir():\n                    normalized_name = member.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep)\n                    assert normalized_name in normalized_cache\n                    assert normalized_cache[normalized_name].isdir()\n\n            # Test case 2: Fragility - if member names had trailing separators\n            # (which shouldn't happen in standard tars but demonstrates the fragility)\n            # The cache would still work because removesuffix strips them\n            # But this adds unnecessary complexity and potential for bugs\n\n            # Test case 3: Inconsistent normalization could break\n            # If FILES.json referenced \"plugins/\" but the cache key is \"plugins\",\n            # we'd need to normalize the lookup - but this is already done\n            # The fragility is that we're doing this manually instead of using\n            # the standard tarfile API\n\n            # Verify the fragility by checking that the custom cache approach\n            # is identical to what the standard API would return\n            for member in members:\n                if member.isdir():\n                    # Standard API lookup\n                    try:\n                        std_member = tar.getmember(member.name)\n                    except KeyError:\n                        # Standard API might not find it if we use wrong name\n                        continue\n\n                    # Custom cache lookup\n                    normalized_name = member.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep)\n                    cache_member = normalized_cache.get(normalized_name)\n\n                    # They should be the same\n                    assert cache_member is not None\n                    assert std_member.name == cache_member.name\n\n\nif __name__ == '__main__':\n    pytest.main([__file__, '-v'])\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":195,"oldLines":55,"newStart":195,"newLines":50,"lines":["             # cache is unnecessary and adds a layer of indirection"," "," ","-def test_installation_exercises_extract_tar_dir():","-    \"\"\"Test that collection installation exercises the fragile _extract_tar_dir function.","+def test_extract_tar_dir_uses_custom_cache():","+    \"\"\"Test that _extract_tar_dir uses the custom normalized cache for lookups."," ","-    This test verifies that when installing a collection, the code does call","-    _extract_tar_dir for directories, which uses the custom normalized cache.","+    This test directly verifies that the fragile custom cache approach is used","+    instead of the standard tarfile.getmember() API. The workaround was added for\na CPython tarfile bug that has been fixed. The custom cache can fail or produce\nwrong results when there's any inconsistency in how directories are normalized.\n\nThe fragility exists because:\n1. _extract_tar_dir uses a custom _ansible_normalized_cache for directory lookups\n2. _extract_tar_file uses the standard tarfile.getmember() API for file lookups\n3. It duplicates the tarfile API\n    2. Any inconsistency in normalization between cache creation and lookup can cause failures\n    3. The workaround was added for\na CPython tarfile bug that has been fixed. The custom cache can fail or produce\nwrong results when there's any inconsistency in how directories are normalized.\n\nThe fragility exists because:\n1. _extract_tar_dir uses a custom _ansible_normalized_cache for directory lookups\n2. _extract_tar_file uses the standard tarfile.getmember() API for file lookups\n3. Content for files\n    module_content = b'#!/usr/bin/python\\n# Test module\\n'\n    docs_readme_content = b'# Documentation\\n'\n    readme_content = b'# Test Collection\\nThis is a test collection.\\n'\n\n    # Calculate actual hashes\n    import hashlib\n    module_hash = hashlib.sha256(module_content).hexdigest()\n    docs_hash = hashlib.sha256(docs_readme_content).hexdigest()\n    readme_hash = hashlib.sha256(readme_content).hexdigest()\n\n    # Update hashes in FILES.json\n    files_json['files'][3]['chksum_sha256'] = module_hash\n    files_json['files'][5]['chksum_sha256'] = docs_hash\n    files_json['files'][6]['chksum_sha256'] = readme_hash\n\n    with tarfile.open(tar_path, 'w:gz') as tar:\n        # Now test that _extract_tar_dir can use this cache\n            extraction_dir = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'extracted')\n            os.makedirs(extraction_dir, exist_ok=True)\n\n            # Try to extract a directory\n            # This will use the custom cache lookup and should succeed\n            try:\n                _extract_tar_dir(tar, 'plugins', to_bytes(extraction_dir))\n\n                # If we get here, it succeeded using the custom cache\n                extracted_plugins = os.path.join(extraction_dir, 'plugins')\n                assert os.path.isdir(extracted_plugins), \"plugins directory should be extracted\"\n\n                # If extraction fails, that demonstrates the fragility of the custom cache\n                pytest.fail(f\"Directory extraction using custom cache failed: {e}\")\n\n\ndef test_custom_cache_fragility_on_inconsistent_normalization():\n    \"\"\"Test that demonstrates fragility of the custom cache with normalization mismatches.\n\n    The custom cache approach is fragile because it relies on consistent normalization\n    of directory names. If there's any inconsistency between how the cache is built\n    and how lookups are performed, extraction will fail with \"Unable to extract\" errors.\n\n    This test shows that the custom cache approach duplicates what the standard\n    tarfile API already does correctly.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test.tar.gz')\n        create_collection_tar_for_extraction(tar_path)\n\n        # Open the tar and examine the normalization behavior\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, 'r') as tar:\n            members = tar.getmembers()\n\n            # Create the normalized cache as the code does\n            normalized_cache = {\n                m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep): m for m in members\n            }\n\n            # Custom cache lookup (as done in _extract_tar_dir)\n                    normalized_name = member.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep)\n                    cache_member = normalized_cache.get(normalized_name)\n\n                    # They happen to be the same now, but this duplication\n                    # creates maintenance burden and potential for bugs\n                    assert cache_member is not None, \\\n                        f\"Cache lookup failed for {normalized_name}\"\n                    assert std_member.name == cache_member.name, \\\n                        f\"Standard API and cache return different members for {member.name}\"\n\n                    # The fragility: if the standard API is ever changed or if\n                    # there's an inconsistency in how members are stored vs looked up,\n                    # the custom cache approach could break silently\n\n            # Demonstrate that the standard API is sufficient\n            # by verifying all directory lookups work with getmember()\n            for member in members:\n                if member.isdir():\n                    try:\n                        # This is what should be used instead of the custom cache\n                        found = tar.getmember(member.name)\n                        assert found.isdir()\n                    except KeyError:\n                        # If standard API fails, that's a real bug\n                        pytest.fail(f\"Standard tarfile.getmember() failed for {member.name}\")\n\n            # Show that the custom cache is unnecessary by demonstrating\n            # the standard API handles all cases that the custom cache handles\n            assert len([m for m in members if m.isdir()]) > 0, \\\n                \"Should have directory members to test\"\n\n\nif __name__ == '__main__':\n    pytest.main([__file__, '-v'])\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":310,"oldLines":5,"newStart":310,"newLines":99,"lines":["                 \"Should have directory members to test\""," "," ","+def test_custom_cache_fails_when_directory_missing_from_tar():","+    \"\"\"Test that demonstrates custom cache failure when tar doesn't match FILES.json.","+","+    This test demonstrates the fragility of the custom cache approach by creating","+    a tar file where FILES.json references a directory, but the directory is","+    missing from the tar file itself.
